<p><i><b>The Simpsons Movie</b></i> is a 2007 American <a href="/wiki/Animation" title="Animation">animated</a> <a href="/wiki/Comedy_film" title="Comedy film">comedy film</a> based on the <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a> television series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons" title="The Simpsons">The Simpsons</a></i>. The film was directed by <a href="/wiki/David_Silverman_(animator)" title="David Silverman (animator)">David Silverman</a>, and stars the regular television cast of <a href="/wiki/Dan_Castellaneta" title="Dan Castellaneta">Dan Castellaneta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julie_Kavner" title="Julie Kavner">Julie Kavner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nancy_Cartwright" title="Nancy Cartwright">Nancy Cartwright</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yeardley_Smith" title="Yeardley Smith">Yeardley Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hank_Azaria" title="Hank Azaria">Hank Azaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Shearer" title="Harry Shearer">Harry Shearer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tress_MacNeille" title="Tress MacNeille">Tress MacNeille</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pamela_Hayden" title="Pamela Hayden">Pamela Hayden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marcia_Wallace" title="Marcia Wallace">Marcia Wallace</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Russi_Taylor" title="Russi Taylor">Russi Taylor</a> with guest appearances by <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hanks" title="Tom Hanks">Tom Hanks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_Day" title="Green Day">Green Day</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Albert_Brooks" title="Albert Brooks">Albert Brooks</a>. The film follows <a href="/wiki/Homer_Simpson" title="Homer Simpson">Homer Simpson</a>, whose irresponsibility gets the better of him when he pollutes the lake in Springfield after the town cleans it up when they had received a warning from the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">Environmental Protection Agency</a>. As the townspeople exile him and eventually his <a href="/wiki/Simpson_family" title="Simpson family">family</a> abandons him, Homer works to redeem his folly by stopping Russ Cargill, the fictional head of the EPA, when he intends to destroy Springfield.</p>
<p>Previous attempts to create a <i>The Simpsons</i> film failed due to the lack of a script of appropriate length and production crew members. Eventually, producers <a href="/wiki/James_L._Brooks" title="James L. Brooks">James L. Brooks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matt_Groening" title="Matt Groening">Matt Groening</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al_Jean" title="Al Jean">Al Jean</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Sakai" title="Richard Sakai">Richard Sakai</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mike_Scully" title="Mike Scully">Mike Scully</a> began development of the film in 2001. A writing team consisting of Brooks, Groening, Jean, Scully, <a href="/wiki/Ian_Maxtone-Graham" title="Ian Maxtone-Graham">Ian Maxtone-Graham</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Meyer" title="George Meyer">George Meyer</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Mirkin" title="David Mirkin">David Mirkin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Reiss" title="Mike Reiss">Mike Reiss</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matt_Selman" title="Matt Selman">Matt Selman</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Swartzwelder" title="John Swartzwelder">John Swartzwelder</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jon_Vitti" title="Jon Vitti">Jon Vitti</a> was assembled. They conceived numerous plot ideas, with Groening's being the one developed into a film. The script was re-written over a hundred times, and this creativity continued after the animation had begun in 2006. This meant hours of finished material was cut, which included <a href="/wiki/Cameo_appearance" title="Cameo appearance">cameo roles</a> from <a href="/wiki/Erin_Brockovich" title="Erin Brockovich">Erin Brockovich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minnie_Driver" title="Minnie Driver">Minnie Driver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isla_Fisher" title="Isla Fisher">Isla Fisher</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kelsey_Grammer" title="Kelsey Grammer">Kelsey Grammer</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Edward_Norton" title="Edward Norton">Edward Norton</a>. Hanks and Green Day appeared in the final cut as themselves.</p>
<p>Tie-in promotions were made with several companies, including <a href="/wiki/Burger_King" title="Burger King">Burger King</a> and <a href="/wiki/7-Eleven" title="7-Eleven">7-Eleven</a>, the latter which <a href="/wiki/Kwik-E-Mart#7-Eleven_promotion" title="Kwik-E-Mart">transformed selected stores</a> into <a href="/wiki/Kwik-E-Mart" title="Kwik-E-Mart">Kwik-E-Marts</a>. The film premiered in <a href="/wiki/Springfield,_Vermont" title="Springfield, Vermont">Springfield, Vermont</a>, which had won the right to hold it through a competition organized by <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a>. The film was a critical and commercial success, grossing over $527 million worldwide.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Simpsons_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Plot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>While performing on <a href="/wiki/Springfield_(The_Simpsons)#Geography.2C_climate.2C_and_environment" title="Springfield (The Simpsons)">Lake Springfield</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Music_group" title="Music group">music group</a> <a href="/wiki/Green_Day" title="Green Day">Green Day</a> perished when the lake's pollution dissolves their barge, following an audience revolt after frontman <a href="/wiki/Billie_Joe_Armstrong" title="Billie Joe Armstrong">Billie Joe Armstrong</a> proposes an environmental discussion. At their memorial, <a href="/wiki/Grampa_Simpson" title="Grampa Simpson">Grampa Simpson</a> foresees the destruction of the town, but only Marge takes this seriously. Later that day, Homer dares his son Bart to skate naked to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Krusty_Burger" title="Krusty Burger">Krusty Burger</a> restaurant and Bart is arrested by <a href="/wiki/Chief_Wiggum" title="Chief Wiggum">Chief Wiggum</a>. Bart considers their neighbor <a href="/wiki/Ned_Flanders" title="Ned Flanders">Ned Flanders</a> a better father figure after Homer refuses to take responsibility for the incident. Lisa and a new Irish friend named <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colin_(The_Simpsons_Movie)" title="Colin (The Simpsons Movie)">Colin</a> convince the entire town to clean their lake.</p>
<p>Meanwhile, Homer adopts a pig from Krusty Burger and names it "<a href="/wiki/Spider-Man" title="Spider-Man">Spider Pig</a>" (later "<a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter" title="Harry Potter">Harry Plopper</a>", and simply "Plopper"), and stores the pig's <a href="/wiki/Feces" title="Feces">feces</a> (and some of his own) in a <a href="/wiki/Silo" title="Silo">silo</a>, until Marge tells him to safely dispose of the waste. Homer initially intends to take his silo to the waste management plant, but after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lenny_Leonard" title="Lenny Leonard">Lenny</a> calls to tell him that <a href="/wiki/Springfield_(The_Simpsons)#Lard_Lad_Donuts" title="Springfield (The Simpsons)">Lard Lad Donuts</a> has been shut down and is giving away free donuts, Homer impatiently dumps the silo straight into the lake, polluting it much worse than before. Moments later, a squirrel jumps into the lake and becomes severely mutated; Flanders and Bart (who bond after Homer humiliates Bart) discover the creature before the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">EPA</a> captures it. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russ_Cargill" title="Russ Cargill">Russ Cargill</a>, head of the EPA, presents five "unthinkable" options to <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">U.S. President</a> <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Schwarzenegger" title="Arnold Schwarzenegger">Arnold Schwarzenegger</a> to keep the town's pollution contained. The slow-witted president picks option 3 without reading it, and Springfield is enclosed in a <a href="/wiki/Domed_city" title="Domed city">large glass dome</a>. When the police discover Homer's silo in the lake, and his responsibility for sealing Springfield in the dome, an angry mob advances on the Simpsons' home to kill Homer, but the family escapes the town through a <a href="/wiki/Sinkhole" title="Sinkhole">sinkhole</a>, which then destroys their house. With the EPA on their trail, the Simpsons flee to <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">Alaska</a>. On the way, Homer tries to make some money at a carnival by riding a motorcycle around the inside of a metal cage.</p>
<p>After three months of futile escape attempts, Springfield's residents finally make a crack in the dome; pointing out the damage, Cargill manipulates Schwarzenegger into ordering the town's destruction. In Alaska, the Simpsons see an advertisement starring <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hanks" title="Tom Hanks">Tom Hanks</a> for a new <a href="/wiki/Grand_Canyon" title="Grand Canyon">Grand Canyon</a> on the site of Springfield; realizing the town is endangered, Marge and the children want to go back to save it, but Homer refuses to help the people who tried to kill him. After failing to talk Homer into it, his family eventually leave him for good. Alone, Homer is stranded on an iceberg and floats away. Meanwhile, Marge and the children are captured by the EPA after a conversation of theirs is overheard by the <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Agency" title="National Security Agency">NSA</a>. After a mysterious <a href="/wiki/Inuit" title="Inuit">Inuit</a> shaman saves him from a <a href="/wiki/Polar_bear" title="Polar bear">polar bear</a>, Homer has an <a href="/wiki/Epiphany_(feeling)" title="Epiphany (feeling)">epiphany</a> and decides to return to Springfield to save the town from danger.</p>
<p>As Homer arrives, a helicopter lowers a small but powerful bomb down a rope through a hole in the dome. The townspeople attempt to climb the rope to escape through the still-opened hole, but Homer slides down the rope and knocks them off along with the bomb. After reconciling with Bart, Homer drives a motorcycle along the dome, inspired by the earlier carnival attraction. As a passenger of the motorcycle, Bart throws the bomb through the hole; seconds later it detonates, shattering the dome and freeing the town. Cargill arrives personally and prepares to shoot Homer and Bart, but Maggie knocks him out with a boulder. The town finally praises and forgives Homer, who rides into the sun rise with Marge and Maggie, whereupon the townspeople restore Springfield to normal. As a symbol of their gratitude, the Simpsons and their friends begin to rebuild the family's house.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Simpsons_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Simpsons_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The production staff had considered a film adaptation of <i>The Simpsons</i> since early in the series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> The show's creator, <a href="/wiki/Matt_Groening" title="Matt Groening">Matt Groening</a>, felt a feature-length film would allow them to increase the show's scale and animate sequences too complex for a TV series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-creators_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-creators-4">[4]</a></sup> He intended the film to be made after the show ended, "but that [...] was undone by good ratings".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-variety_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-variety-5">[5]</a></sup> There were attempts to adapt the <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_4)" title="The Simpsons (season 4)">fourth season</a> episode "<a href="/wiki/Kamp_Krusty" title="Kamp Krusty">Kamp Krusty</a>" into a film, but difficulties were encountered in expanding the episode to feature-length.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> For a long time the project was held up. There was difficulty finding a story that was sufficient for a film, and the crew did not have enough time to complete such a project, as they already worked full-time on the show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-avclub_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-avclub-7">[7]</a></sup> Groening also expressed a wish to make <i>Simpstasia</i>, a parody of <i><a href="/wiki/Fantasia_(1940_film)" title="Fantasia (1940 film)">Fantasia</a></i>; it was never produced, partly because it would have been too difficult to write a feature-length script.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> Before his death, <a href="/wiki/Phil_Hartman" title="Phil Hartman">Phil Hartman</a> had said he had wished to make a live action <a href="/wiki/Troy_McClure" title="Troy McClure">Troy McClure</a> film, and several of the show's staff had expressed a desire to help create it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<table cellspacing="5" class="toccolours" style="float: right; margin-left: 1em; margin-right: 2em; font-size: 85%; background:#c6dbf7; color:black; width:28em; max-width: 40%;">
<tr>
<td style="text-align: left;">"If every episode of <i>The Simpsons</i> is a celebration, which we try to make it, then the movie is like a big celebration. It's a way of honoring the animators, allowing them to really strut their stuff and really go as far as they can with the art of the handwritten gesture. It's a way of honoring the writers, because we were able to get the best all-star writers of <i>The Simpsons</i> and write our hearts out, and it's a way of honoring all the great actors."</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="text-align: left;">— Matt Groening<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-creators_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-creators-4">[4]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The voice cast was signed on to do the film in 2001,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-empire_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-empire-10">[10]</a></sup> and work then began on the script.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usa_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-usa-11">[11]</a></sup> The producers were initially worried that creating a film would have a negative effect on the series, as they did not have enough crew to focus their attention on both projects. As the series progressed, additional writers and animators were hired so that both the show and the film could be produced at the same time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-officialsite_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-officialsite-12">[12]</a></sup> Groening and <a href="/wiki/James_L._Brooks" title="James L. Brooks">James L. Brooks</a> invited back <a href="/wiki/Mike_Scully" title="Mike Scully">Mike Scully</a> and <a href="/wiki/Al_Jean" title="Al Jean">Al Jean</a> (who continued to work as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Show_runner" title="Show runner">showrunner</a> on the television series) to produce the film with them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pig_feces_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-pig_feces-13">[13]</a></sup> They then signed <a href="/wiki/David_Silverman_(animator)" title="David Silverman (animator)">David Silverman</a> (who, in anticipation of the project, had quit his job at <a href="/wiki/Pixar" title="Pixar">Pixar</a>) to direct the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pig_feces_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-pig_feces-13">[13]</a></sup> The "strongest possible" writing team was assembled, with many of the writers from the show's early seasons being chosen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-officialsite_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-officialsite-12">[12]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Mirkin" title="David Mirkin">David Mirkin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Reiss" title="Mike Reiss">Mike Reiss</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Meyer" title="George Meyer">George Meyer</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Swartzwelder" title="John Swartzwelder">John Swartzwelder</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jon_Vitti" title="Jon Vitti">Jon Vitti</a> were selected. <a href="/wiki/Ian_Maxtone-Graham" title="Ian Maxtone-Graham">Ian Maxtone-Graham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Matt_Selman" title="Matt Selman">Matt Selman</a> joined later, and Brooks, Groening, Scully, and Jean also wrote parts of the script.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-officialsite_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-officialsite-12">[12]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sam_Simon" title="Sam Simon">Sam Simon</a> did not return having left the show over creative differences in 1993. Former writer <a href="/wiki/Conan_O%27Brien" title="Conan O'Brien">Conan O'Brien</a> expressed interest in working with the <i>Simpsons</i> staff again, although he later joked that "I worry that the <i>Simpsons</i>-writing portion of my brain has been destroyed after 14 years of talking to <a href="/wiki/Lindsay_Lohan" title="Lindsay Lohan">Lindsay Lohan</a> and that guy from <i><a href="/wiki/One_Tree_Hill_(TV_series)" title="One Tree Hill (TV series)">One Tree Hill</a></i>, so maybe it's all for the best."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The same went for director <a href="/wiki/Brad_Bird" title="Brad Bird">Brad Bird</a> who said he had "entertained fantasies of asking if [he] could work on the movie", but did not have enough time due to work on <i><a href="/wiki/Ratatouille_(film)" title="Ratatouille (film)">Ratatouille</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-empire_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-empire-10">[10]</a></sup> The producers arranged a deal with Fox that would allow them to abandon production of the film at any point if they felt the script was unsatisfactory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Work continued on the screenplay from 2003 onwards,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-15">[15]</a></sup> taking place in the small bungalow where Groening first pitched <i>The Simpsons</i> in 1987.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-totalfilm_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-totalfilm-16">[16]</a></sup> The writers spent six months discussing a plot,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tislondon_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-tislondon-17">[17]</a></sup> and each of them offered sketchy ideas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-totalfilm_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-totalfilm-16">[16]</a></sup> Jean suggested the family rescue <a href="/wiki/Manatee" title="Manatee">manatees</a>, which became the 2005 episode "<a href="/wiki/The_Bonfire_of_the_Manatees" title="The Bonfire of the Manatees">The Bonfire of the Manatees</a>", and there was also a notion similar to that of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Truman_Show" title="The Truman Show">The Truman Show</a></i> where the characters discovered their lives were a TV show. Groening rejected this, as he felt that the Simpsons should "never become aware of themselves as celebrities".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-empire_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-empire-10">[10]</a></sup> Groening read about a town that had to get rid of pig feces in their water supply, which inspired the plot of the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pig_feces_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-pig_feces-13">[13]</a></sup> The decision for <a href="/wiki/Ned_Flanders" title="Ned Flanders">Flanders</a> to have an important role also came early on, as Jean wished to see Bart wonder what his life would be like if Flanders were his father.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moviesonline_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-moviesonline-18">[18]</a></sup> Having eventually decided on the basic outline of the plot for the film, the writers then separated it into seven sections. Jean, Scully, Reiss, Swartzwelder, Vitti, Mirkin, and Meyer wrote 25 pages each, and the group met one month later to merge the seven sections into one "very rough draft".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-officialsite_12-3"><a href="#cite_note-officialsite-12">[12]</a></sup> The film's script was written in the same way as the television series: the writers sitting around a table, pitching ideas, and trying to make each other laugh.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-15">[15]</a></sup> The script went through over 100 revisions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tislondon_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-tislondon-17">[17]</a></sup> and at one point the film was a musical. However, the songs were continually being shortened and the idea was dropped.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Groening described his desire to also make the film dramatically stronger than a TV episode, saying that he wanted to "give you something that you haven't seen before".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Animation">Animation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Simpsons_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Animation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:David_Silverman_in_2007-cropped.JPG"><img alt="A man with a cowboy hat on his back." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="475" data-file-width="349" height="231" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/David_Silverman_in_2007-cropped.JPG/170px-David_Silverman_in_2007-cropped.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/David_Silverman_in_2007-cropped.JPG/255px-David_Silverman_in_2007-cropped.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/David_Silverman_in_2007-cropped.JPG/340px-David_Silverman_in_2007-cropped.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:David_Silverman_in_2007-cropped.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Director <a href="/wiki/David_Silverman_(animator)" title="David Silverman (animator)">David Silverman</a> looked at some of the television episodes he had directed for inspiration.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Animation for the film began in January 2006,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pig_feces_13-3"><a href="#cite_note-pig_feces-13">[13]</a></sup> with the <i><a href="/wiki/The_Itchy_%26_Scratchy_Show" title="The Itchy &amp; Scratchy Show">Itchy &amp; Scratchy</a></i> short being the first scene to be <a href="/wiki/Storyboard" title="Storyboard">storyboarded</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> Groening rejected making either a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Live-action" title="Live-action">live-action</a> or a <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">CGI</a> film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-totalfilm_16-2"><a href="#cite_note-totalfilm-16">[16]</a></sup> calling the film's animation "deliberately imperfect" and "a tribute to the art of <a href="/wiki/Traditional_animation" title="Traditional animation">hand-drawn animation</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The film was produced in a widescreen <a href="/wiki/Anamorphic_format" title="Anamorphic format">2.35:1</a> aspect ratio, to distinguish it from the look of the television series,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-officialsite_12-4"><a href="#cite_note-officialsite-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> and colored with the largest palette the animators had ever had available to them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-creators_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-creators-4">[4]</a></sup> A lot of the animation was produced using <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cintiq" title="Cintiq">Wacom Cintiq</a> tablets, which allowed images to be drawn directly onto a computer monitor to facilitate production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> Animation production work was divided among four studios around the world: <a href="/wiki/Film_Roman" title="Film Roman">Film Roman</a> in <a href="/wiki/Burbank,_California" title="Burbank, California">Burbank, California</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rough_Draft_Studios" title="Rough Draft Studios">Rough Draft Studios</a> in <a href="/wiki/Glendale,_California" title="Glendale, California">Glendale, California</a>, and <a href="/wiki/AKOM" title="AKOM">AKOM</a> and Rough Draft's division in <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>, South Korea. As with the television series, the storyboarding, characters, background layout, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Animatic" title="Animatic">animatic</a> parts of production, were done in America. The overseas studios completed the <a href="/wiki/Inbetweening" title="Inbetweening">inbetweening</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Digital_ink_and_paint" title="Digital ink and paint">digital ink and paint</a>, and rendered the animation to tape before being shipped back to the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com2_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-com2-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>Director <a href="/wiki/David_Silverman_(animator)" title="David Silverman (animator)">David Silverman</a> said that unlike the TV series where "you [have] to pick and choose", the film gave them the opportunity to "lavish that attention [on] every single scene". The characters have shadows, unlike in the show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes_15-3"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-15">[15]</a></sup> Silverman and the animators looked to films such as <i><a href="/wiki/The_Incredibles" title="The Incredibles">The Incredibles</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Triplets_of_Belleville" title="The Triplets of Belleville">The Triplets of Belleville</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Bad_Day_at_Black_Rock" title="Bad Day at Black Rock">Bad Day at Black Rock</a></i> for inspiration, as they were "a great education in staging because of how the characters are placed".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes_15-4"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-15">[15]</a></sup> They also looked for ideas for a dream sequence, in Disney films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Dumbo" title="Dumbo">Dumbo</a></i> and the <a href="/wiki/Pluto_(Disney)" title="Pluto (Disney)">Pluto</a> cartoon <i>Pluto's Judgment Day</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-totalfilm_16-3"><a href="#cite_note-totalfilm-16">[16]</a></sup> and for crowd scenes in <i><a href="/wiki/It%27s_a_Mad,_Mad,_Mad,_Mad_World" title="It's a Mad, Mad, Mad, Mad World">It's a Mad, Mad, Mad, Mad World</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moviesonline_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-moviesonline-18">[18]</a></sup> Silverman looked at some of the <i>Simpsons</i> episodes he had directed, primarily his two favorites, "<a href="/wiki/Homie_the_Clown" title="Homie the Clown">Homie the Clown</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Three_Men_and_a_Comic_Book" title="Three Men and a Comic Book">Three Men and a Comic Book</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-silvermaninter_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-silvermaninter-24">[24]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mike_B._Anderson" title="Mike B. Anderson">Mike B. Anderson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lauren_MacMullan" title="Lauren MacMullan">Lauren MacMullan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rich_Moore" title="Rich Moore">Rich Moore</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Steven_Dean_Moore" title="Steven Dean Moore">Steven Dean Moore</a> each directed the animation for around a quarter of the film under Silverman's supervision, with numerous other animators working on scenes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com2_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-com2-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Casting">Casting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Simpsons_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Casting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_The_Simpsons_cast_members" title="List of The Simpsons cast members">List of The Simpsons cast members</a></div>
<p>For inspiration for the crowd scenes in the film, the production staff referenced a poster featuring more than 320 <i>Simpsons</i> characters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ew_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-ew-25">[25]</a></sup> Groening said they tried to include every single character in the film, with 98 having speaking parts,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pig_feces_13-4"><a href="#cite_note-pig_feces-13">[13]</a></sup> and most members of the crowds being previously established characters instead of generic people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-3"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> The series' regular voice actors: <a href="/wiki/Dan_Castellaneta" title="Dan Castellaneta">Dan Castellaneta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Julie_Kavner" title="Julie Kavner">Julie Kavner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nancy_Cartwright" title="Nancy Cartwright">Nancy Cartwright</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yeardley_Smith" title="Yeardley Smith">Yeardley Smith</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hank_Azaria" title="Hank Azaria">Hank Azaria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Harry_Shearer" title="Harry Shearer">Harry Shearer</a>, as well as semi-regular performers <a href="/wiki/Tress_MacNeille" title="Tress MacNeille">Tress MacNeille</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pamela_Hayden" title="Pamela Hayden">Pamela Hayden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marcia_Wallace" title="Marcia Wallace">Marcia Wallace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maggie_Roswell" title="Maggie Roswell">Maggie Roswell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russi_Taylor" title="Russi Taylor">Russi Taylor</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Karl_Wiedergott" title="Karl Wiedergott">Karl Wiedergott</a>, reprised their roles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-variety_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-variety-5">[5]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Joe_Mantegna" title="Joe Mantegna">Joe Mantegna</a> returned as <a href="/wiki/Fat_Tony_(The_Simpsons)" title="Fat Tony (The Simpsons)">Fat Tony</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fattony_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-fattony-26">[26]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Albert_Brooks" title="Albert Brooks">Albert Brooks</a>, who supplied many guest voices in episodes, was hired as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_one-time_characters_in_The_Simpsons#The_Simpsons_Movie" title="List of one-time characters in The Simpsons">Russ Cargill</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-officialsite_12-5"><a href="#cite_note-officialsite-12">[12]</a></sup> after he told the staff that he wanted to be part of the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moviesonline_18-2"><a href="#cite_note-moviesonline-18">[18]</a></sup> For "about a week", he was to reprise the role of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_one-time_characters_in_The_Simpsons#Season_8" title="List of one-time characters in The Simpsons">Hank Scorpio</a> from the episode "<a href="/wiki/You_Only_Move_Twice" title="You Only Move Twice">You Only Move Twice</a>", but the staff felt that creating a new character was a better idea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com2_23-2"><a href="#cite_note-com2-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Simpsons_angry_mob.png"><img alt="Lots of angry people holding flaming torches as they march together" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="126" data-file-width="300" height="126" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/a/ab/Simpsons_angry_mob.png" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">The shot of an angry mob coming for Homer features cameos from more than 320 characters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tislondon_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-tislondon-17">[17]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The cast did the first of three table readings in May 2005,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-variety_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-variety-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> and began recording every week from June 2006 until the end of production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> James L. Brooks directed them for the first time since the television show's early seasons. Castellaneta found the recording sessions "more intense" than recording the television series, and "more emotionally dramatic".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Some scenes, such as Marge's video message to Homer, were recorded over one hundred times, leaving the voice cast exhausted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moviesonline_18-3"><a href="#cite_note-moviesonline-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>The writers had written the opening concert scene without a specific band in mind. <a href="/wiki/Green_Day" title="Green Day">Green Day</a> were cast in that role having requested to guest star in the show. <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hanks" title="Tom Hanks">Tom Hanks</a> also appears as himself in the film and accepted the offer after just one phone call.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moviesonline_18-4"><a href="#cite_note-moviesonline-18">[18]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Everybody_Loves_Raymond" title="Everybody Loves Raymond">Everybody Loves Raymond</a></i> creator <a href="/wiki/Philip_Rosenthal" title="Philip Rosenthal">Philip Rosenthal</a> provides the voice of the father in the "new <a href="/wiki/Grand_Canyon" title="Grand Canyon">Grand Canyon</a>" commercial with Hanks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-4"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> Due to time restraints, several guests who had recorded parts were cut from the film. <a href="/wiki/Minnie_Driver" title="Minnie Driver">Minnie Driver</a> recorded the part of a patronizing grievance counselor in a scene that ended up being cut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-drivercut_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-drivercut-30">[30]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Edward_Norton" title="Edward Norton">Edward Norton</a> recorded the part of the man who gets crushed as the dome is implemented, performing a <a href="/wiki/Woody_Allen" title="Woody Allen">Woody Allen</a> impression. The staff felt the voice was too distracting, so Castellaneta re-recorded Norton's dialogue with a different voice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-5"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Isla_Fisher" title="Isla Fisher">Isla Fisher</a> and <a href="/wiki/Erin_Brockovich" title="Erin Brockovich">Erin Brockovich</a> also recorded cameos, but their scenes were cut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pig_feces_13-5"><a href="#cite_note-pig_feces-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kelsey_Grammer" title="Kelsey Grammer">Kelsey Grammer</a> recorded lines for <a href="/wiki/Sideshow_Bob" title="Sideshow Bob">Sideshow Bob</a>, who was to appear at several different points,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-6"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com2_23-3"><a href="#cite_note-com2-23">[23]</a></sup> but these scenes were also cut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moviesonline_18-5"><a href="#cite_note-moviesonline-18">[18]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Knoxville" title="Johnny Knoxville">Johnny Knoxville</a> was also touted as a possible guest star.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moviesonline_18-6"><a href="#cite_note-moviesonline-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although he does not provide the voice, <a href="/wiki/Arnold_Schwarzenegger" title="Arnold Schwarzenegger">Arnold Schwarzenegger</a> is <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President of the United States</a> rather than then-President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> because, according to Groening, "in two years ... the film [would be] out of date".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tislondon_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-tislondon-17">[17]</a></sup> Brooks was nervous about the idea, noting that "[Schwarzenegger's] opinion polls were way down", and has said that they "were [hoping] he'd make a political comeback".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-creators_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-creators-4">[4]</a></sup> The animators began by drawing an accurate caricature of Schwarzenegger,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moviesonline_18-7"><a href="#cite_note-moviesonline-18">[18]</a></sup> but one of the staff instead suggested an altered version of recurring character <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rainer_Wolfcastle" title="Rainer Wolfcastle">Rainier Wolfcastle</a> as President.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-silvermaninter_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-silvermaninter-24">[24]</a></sup> This idea was developed, with the design of Wolfcastle, himself also a caricature of Schwarzenegger, being given more wrinkles under his eyes and a different hairstyle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moviesonline_18-8"><a href="#cite_note-moviesonline-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Editing">Editing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Simpsons_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Editing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Every aspect of the film was constantly analyzed, with storylines, jokes, and characters regularly being rewritten.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-7"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> Although most animated films do not make extensive changes to the film during active production due to budget restrictions,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-empire_10-3"><a href="#cite_note-empire-10">[10]</a></sup> <i>The Simpsons Movie</i> crew continued to edit their film into 2007, with some edits taking place as late as May, two months before the film was released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-8"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> James L. Brooks noted, "70 percent of the things in [one of the trailers]—based on where we were eight weeks ago—are no longer in the movie."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ew_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-ew-25">[25]</a></sup> Groening said that enough material for two more movies was cut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-totalfilm_16-4"><a href="#cite_note-totalfilm-16">[16]</a></sup> Various new characters were created, and then cut because they did not contribute enough.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-empire_10-4"><a href="#cite_note-empire-10">[10]</a></sup> Originally Marge was the character who had the <a href="/wiki/Prophecy" title="Prophecy">prophetic vision</a> in church. The writers however considered this to be too dark and it was changed to Grampa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-9"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> The role of Lisa's love interest Colin was frequently revised. He was previously named Dexter and Adrien, and his appearance was completely altered.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moviesonline_18-9"><a href="#cite_note-moviesonline-18">[18]</a></sup> One idea was to have <a href="/wiki/Milhouse_Van_Houten" title="Milhouse Van Houten">Milhouse</a> act as Lisa's love interest, but the writers realized "the audience was not as familiar with [his] long-standing crush on [Lisa] as [they had] thought".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-10"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Car_chase" title="Car chase">car chase</a> in which Homer throws flaming <a href="/wiki/Mummy" title="Mummy">mummies</a> out of a truck at the EPA was replaced with "more emotional and realistic" scenes at the motel and carnival that allowed for a change of pace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-11"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>Further changes were made after the March 2007 preview screenings of the film in <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">Portland, Oregon</a> and <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-12"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> This included the deletion of <a href="/wiki/Kang_and_Kodos" title="Kang and Kodos">Kang and Kodos</a> heavily criticizing the film during the end credits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pig_feces_13-6"><a href="#cite_note-pig_feces-13">[13]</a></sup> A lot of people at the screenings found the original film too coarse, and some of Homer's behavior too unkind, so several scenes were toned down to make him appear nicer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-13"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> Russ Cargill was redesigned several times, originally appearing as an older man whose speech patterns Albert Brooks based on <a href="/wiki/Donald_Rumsfeld" title="Donald Rumsfeld">Donald Rumsfeld</a>. The older model was the one used by <a href="/wiki/Burger_King" title="Burger King">Burger King</a> for the action figure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-14"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> Cargill's scene with Bart and Homer at the film's conclusion was added in to fully resolve his story, and the "<a href="/wiki/List_of_recurring_The_Simpsons_characters#Plopper" title="List of recurring The Simpsons characters">Spider-Pig</a>" gag was also a late addition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moviesonline_18-10"><a href="#cite_note-moviesonline-18">[18]</a></sup> One excised scene, before the dome is put over Springfield, had <a href="/wiki/Mr._Burns" title="Mr. Burns">Mr. Burns</a> reminding viewers that it was the last point in the film that they could get a refund.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-15"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> Other deletions included Homer's encounter with a sausage truck driver, which was featured on the DVD, a scene with Plopper the pig at the end,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ploppersback_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-ploppersback-32">[32]</a></sup> and a news report, showing the dome's effect on daily life in Springfield in areas such as farming and sport, was cut because it did not fit the overall context of the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-16"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> Several musical numbers, at various intervals throughout the film, were cut.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-17"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> These included a song about Alaska, featuring music by <a href="/wiki/David_A._Stewart" title="David A. Stewart">Dave Stewart</a> of <a href="/wiki/Eurythmics" title="Eurythmics">Eurythmics</a>. Jean said it "got pretty far along in the animation, and then we got scared that the movie began to drag in that section."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Simpsons_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_Movie:_The_Music" title="The Simpsons Movie: The Music">The Simpsons Movie: The Music</a></div>
<p>James L. Brooks chose <a href="/wiki/Hans_Zimmer" title="Hans Zimmer">Hans Zimmer</a> to compose the film's score, as they were good friends and regular collaborators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-post_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-post-35">[35]</a></sup> Zimmer felt that the score was a "unique challenge", and he had to "try and express the style of <i>The Simpsons</i> without wearing the audience out".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> He used <a href="/wiki/Danny_Elfman" title="Danny Elfman">Danny Elfman</a>'s original <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_Theme" title="The Simpsons Theme">opening theme</a>, but did not wish to overuse it. He created themes for each member of the family. Homer's <a href="/wiki/Leitmotif" title="Leitmotif">leitmotif</a> was a major focus, and Zimmer also composed smaller themes for Bart and Marge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oneandonly_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-oneandonly-37">[37]</a></sup> Regular television series composer <a href="/wiki/Alf_Clausen" title="Alf Clausen">Alf Clausen</a> was not asked to score the film, noting: "sometimes you're the windshield, sometimes you're the bug".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to their appearance in the film, <a href="/wiki/Green_Day" title="Green Day">Green Day</a> recorded its own version of the <i>Simpsons</i> theme, and released it as <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_Theme#Alternative_versions" title="The Simpsons Theme">a single</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hr_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-hr-39">[39]</a></sup> Zimmer turned the Spider-Pig song into a choral piece, which was a joke he never intended to be put into the film. Zimmer also had to write foreign-language lyrics for the 32 <a href="/wiki/Dubbing_(filmmaking)" title="Dubbing (filmmaking)">dubbed</a> versions of the song when the film was released internationally. He found translating the song into Spanish the hardest to write. The same choir learned to sing the piece for each of the foreign-language dubs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oneandonly_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-oneandonly-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Themes">Themes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Simpsons_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Themes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lisacolinappletree.png"><img alt="A girl looks nervous as she looks at the boy next to her. An apple tree is in the background." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="135" data-file-width="325" height="91" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/89/Lisacolinappletree.png/220px-Lisacolinappletree.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/89/Lisacolinappletree.png 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lisacolinappletree.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An apple tree was inserted into the background here, in reference to <a href="/wiki/Adam_and_Eve" title="Adam and Eve">Adam and Eve</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Garden_of_Eden" title="Garden of Eden">Garden of Eden</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com2_23-4"><a href="#cite_note-com2-23">[23]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Al Jean described the film's message as being "a man should listen to his wife". In addition, the film parodies two major contemporary issues, religion and environmentalism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-breath_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-breath-40">[40]</a></sup> The theme of environmentalism is present throughout the film: in Homer's polluting of Lake Springfield, Green Day's cameo, Lisa's activism and her romance with Colin. The villainous Russ Cargill is head of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="Environmental Protection Agency">Environmental Protection Agency</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pig_feces_13-7"><a href="#cite_note-pig_feces-13">[13]</a></sup> Reviewer Ed Gonzalez argued the plot was a satire of the government's reaction to the effects of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina" title="Hurricane Katrina">Hurricane Katrina</a> on <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gonzalez_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-gonzalez-41">[41]</a></sup> Ian Nathan of <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i> magazine criticized this focus, believing it gave the film an "overt political agenda [which] border[s] on <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/polemic" title="wikt:polemic">polemic</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-empirereview_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-empirereview-42">[42]</a></sup> James D. Bloom of <a href="/wiki/Muhlenberg_College" title="Muhlenberg College">Muhlenberg College</a> commented on the "explicitness" of the film's "<i>intellectual</i> agenda", on this issue, shown particularly through Lisa. He wrote that the film's first post-opening credits scene, which sees Green Day fail in an attempt to engage their audience on the issue of the environment, "sets in motion a plot expressly built around cultural agenda-setting" and "reflection on timely 'issues'."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>Religion is focused on in Grampa's momentary possession, and Marge believing what he said to be a message from God.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-44">[44]</a></sup> Groening joked the film "posit[s] the existence of a very active God", when asked if he believed it was likely to offend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-breath_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-breath-40">[40]</a></sup> Mark I. Pinsky, author of <i>The Gospel According to The Simpsons</i>, said the film "treats genuine faith with respect, while keeping a sharp eye out for religious pretension and hypocrisy of all kinds". Regarding the scene where the tenants of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moe%27s_Tavern" title="Moe's Tavern">Moe's Tavern</a> and the Church switch locations, he believed it took the "chance to unmask everyone's human fallibility." In analyzing the role of Ned Flanders, he wrote, "It is [the] willingness of <i>The Simpsons</i> to depict all the different sides of us [...] that makes it so rich and funny on our complicated relationship with religion."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Trees are a <a href="/wiki/Motif_(narrative)" title="Motif (narrative)">motif</a> in the film, and they were implemented in every important or emotional scene throughout the film. The animators inserted an apple tree behind Lisa and Colin during their initial meeting, a reference to the biblical figures of <a href="/wiki/Adam_and_Eve" title="Adam and Eve">Adam and Eve</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Garden_of_Eden" title="Garden of Eden">Garden of Eden</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com2_23-5"><a href="#cite_note-com2-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_references">Cultural references</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Simpsons_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Cultural references">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Many cultural references and allusions are made throughout the film. <a href="/wiki/Green_Day" title="Green Day">Green Day</a> play "<a href="/wiki/Nearer,_My_God,_to_Thee" title="Nearer, My God, to Thee">Nearer, My God, to Thee</a>" on violins as their barge sinks, in a sequence parodying the film <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-18"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-46">[46]</a></sup> When Bart is riding his skateboard naked, different passing objects are constantly covering his <a href="/wiki/Sex_organ" title="Sex organ">genitalia</a>, a nod to similar techniques used in <i><a href="/wiki/Austin_Powers:_International_Man_of_Mystery" title="Austin Powers: International Man of Mystery">Austin Powers: International Man of Mystery</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com2_23-6"><a href="#cite_note-com2-23">[23]</a></sup> Homer and Marge's love scene parodies many <a href="/wiki/The_Walt_Disney_Company" title="The Walt Disney Company">Disney</a> films, including <i><a href="/wiki/Cinderella_(1950_film)" title="Cinderella (1950 film)">Cinderella</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-totalfilm_16-5"><a href="#cite_note-totalfilm-16">[16]</a></sup> with Disney-style animals helping them undress.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moviesonline_18-11"><a href="#cite_note-moviesonline-18">[18]</a></sup> Originally, the music from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wizard_of_Oz_(1939_film)" title="The Wizard of Oz (1939 film)">The Wizard of Oz</a></i> was used in that scene, and the <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">fawn</a> had white spots; these were removed because the animators felt it resembled <a href="/wiki/Bambi_(character)" title="Bambi (character)">Bambi</a> too clearly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-19"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> Bart impersonates <a href="/wiki/Mickey_Mouse" title="Mickey Mouse">Mickey Mouse</a> on the train, calling himself "the mascot of an evil corporation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moviesonline_18-12"><a href="#cite_note-moviesonline-18">[18]</a></sup> Homer plays <i>Grand Theft Walrus</i>, an allusion to the <a href="/wiki/Video_game" title="Video game">video game</a> series <i><a href="/wiki/Grand_Theft_Auto" title="Grand Theft Auto">Grand Theft Auto</a></i>. In the game, his character shoots a tap-dancing penguin in reference to the film <i><a href="/wiki/Happy_Feet" title="Happy Feet">Happy Feet</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-20"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> The "Spider-Pig" song is a parody of the <a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_(theme_song)" title="Spider-Man (theme song)">theme song</a> of the 1967 <i><a href="/wiki/Spider-Man_(1967_TV_series)" title="Spider-Man (1967 TV series)">Spider-Man</a></i> TV series,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oneandonly_37-2"><a href="#cite_note-oneandonly-37">[37]</a></sup> and the name of Lisa's lecture is <i>An Irritating Truth</i>, a play on <a href="/wiki/Al_Gore" title="Al Gore">Al Gore</a>'s film <i><a href="/wiki/An_Inconvenient_Truth" title="An Inconvenient Truth">An Inconvenient Truth</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters_44-1"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-44">[44]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Remote_control_vehicle" title="Remote control vehicle">bomb disposal robot</a> was based on <a href="/wiki/Vincent_D%27Onofrio" title="Vincent D'Onofrio">Vincent D'Onofrio</a>'s character Leonard "Pyle" Lawrence from the film <i><a href="/wiki/Full_Metal_Jacket" title="Full Metal Jacket">Full Metal Jacket</a></i>, who commits suicide in a similar way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com2_23-7"><a href="#cite_note-com2-23">[23]</a></sup> At the end of the film, the crowd's celebration is similar to the conclusion of <i><a href="/wiki/Return_of_the_Jedi" title="Return of the Jedi">Return of the Jedi</a></i>, with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carl_Carlson" title="Carl Carlson">Carl</a> performing exactly the same hand gestures as <a href="/wiki/Lando_Calrissian" title="Lando Calrissian">Lando Calrissian</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com2_23-8"><a href="#cite_note-com2-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>The $1,000 Homer received when entering Alaska is a reference to the <a href="/wiki/Alaska_Permanent_Fund" title="Alaska Permanent Fund">Alaska Permanent Fund Dividend</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> As Homer leaves Eski-Moe's he grabs on to a passing truck and uses it to propel himself back to the house, a tribute to actor <a href="/wiki/Buster_Keaton" title="Buster Keaton">Buster Keaton</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-21"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> while the epiphany scene features homages to the film <i><a href="/wiki/Brazil_(1985_film)" title="Brazil (1985 film)">Brazil</a></i> and the works of <a href="/wiki/Salvador_Dal%C3%AD" title="Salvador Dalí">Salvador Dalí</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com2_23-9"><a href="#cite_note-com2-23">[23]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> appears as Itchy's vice president, while an <a href="/wiki/Orc_(Middle-earth)" title="Orc (Middle-earth)">Orc</a> from <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings" title="The Lord of the Rings">The Lord of the Rings</a></i> appears in the mob scene.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-22"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> A scene that was cut had Marge and the kids appear on the TV talk show <i><a href="/wiki/The_View_(U.S._TV_series)" title="The View (U.S. TV series)">The View</a></i> to spread the news of Springfield's impending doom. Parts were written for the show's entire panel and the scene was planned to feature Russ Cargill having a gunfight with <a href="/wiki/Joy_Behar" title="Joy Behar">Joy Behar</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-23"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> Another dropped scene featured <a href="/wiki/Moe_Szyslak" title="Moe Szyslak">Moe</a> describing Springfield's varying physical states inside the dome, one of which was the <a href="/wiki/Disneyland" title="Disneyland">Disneyland</a> ride <a href="/wiki/Autopia" title="Autopia">Autopia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-24"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup> There are several references to events in previous TV episodes of <i>The Simpsons</i>. These include the wreckage of the ambulance from the episode "<a href="/wiki/Bart_the_Daredevil" title="Bart the Daredevil">Bart the Daredevil</a>" crashed into a tree next to Springfield Gorge.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moviesonline_18-13"><a href="#cite_note-moviesonline-18">[18]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Carpenters" title="The Carpenters">The Carpenters</a>' song "<a href="/wiki/(They_Long_to_Be)_Close_to_You" title="(They Long to Be) Close to You">(They Long to Be) Close to You</a>" was used in Homer and Marge's wedding video and had also been used in several emotional moments between them in the TV series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-com_21-25"><a href="#cite_note-com-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Simpsons_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SimpsonsMarquee.jpg"><img alt='A board reads "Welcome to the Hometown Springfield Premiere of The Simpsons Movie' class="thumbimage" data-file-height="288" data-file-width="384" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/SimpsonsMarquee.jpg/220px-SimpsonsMarquee.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/SimpsonsMarquee.jpg/330px-SimpsonsMarquee.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8f/SimpsonsMarquee.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SimpsonsMarquee.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Marquee_(sign)" title="Marquee (sign)">Marquee</a> from the film's premiere, which took place in <a href="/wiki/Springfield,_Vermont" title="Springfield, Vermont">Springfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>20th Century Fox announced on April 1, 2006 that the film would be released worldwide on July 27, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> The film was released a day earlier in Australia and the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> Little information about the plot was released in the weeks building up to the film's release. Groening did not feel that "people look in the TV section of the newspaper and think, 'I'll watch this week's <i>Simpsons</i> because I like the plot.' You just tune in and see what happens."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-empire_10-5"><a href="#cite_note-empire-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Fox held a competition among 16 <a href="/wiki/Springfield_(toponym)" title="Springfield (toponym)">Springfields</a> across the United States to host the American premiere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> Each Springfield produced a film, explaining why their town should host the premiere, with the results being decided via a vote on the <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i> website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-verm_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-verm-54">[54]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Springfield,_Minnesota" title="Springfield, Minnesota">Springfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Minnesota" title="Minnesota">Minnesota</a> dropped out on May 31, 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The winner was announced on July 10 to be <a href="/wiki/Springfield,_Vermont" title="Springfield, Vermont">Springfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">Vermont</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-launch_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-launch-56">[56]</a></sup> The town beat <a href="/wiki/Springfield,_Illinois" title="Springfield, Illinois">Springfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illinois" title="Illinois">Illinois</a> by 15,367 votes to 14,634. Each of the other 14 entrants held their own smaller screenings of the film on July 26.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-verm_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-verm-54">[54]</a></sup> Springfield, Vermont hosted the world premiere of the film on July 21 with a yellow carpet instead of the traditional <a href="/wiki/Red_carpet" title="Red carpet">red</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-launch_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-launch-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>The film was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PG-Rating" title="PG-Rating">rated PG-13</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Motion_Picture_Association_of_America" title="Motion Picture Association of America">Motion Picture Association of America</a> for "irreverent humor throughout".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> The production staff had expected this rating.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-usa_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-usa-11">[11]</a></sup> However, the <a href="/wiki/British_Board_of_Film_Classification" title="British Board of Film Classification">British Board of Film Classification</a> passed the film as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/12_certificate" title="12 certificate">PG</a> with no cuts made.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbfc_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbfc-58">[58]</a></sup> A BBFC spokeswoman said regarding Bart's brief nude scene, "natural <a href="/wiki/Nudity" title="Nudity">nudity</a> with no sexual content is acceptable in PG films".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Simpsons_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Marketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kwik-e-mart-7-11.jpg"><img alt="A building with striped lines across it, some people stand in front of it" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="698" data-file-width="1143" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Kwik-e-mart-7-11.jpg/220px-Kwik-e-mart-7-11.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Kwik-e-mart-7-11.jpg/330px-Kwik-e-mart-7-11.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Kwik-e-mart-7-11.jpg/440px-Kwik-e-mart-7-11.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kwik-e-mart-7-11.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/7-Eleven" title="7-Eleven">7-Eleven</a> store in <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a> transformed into a <a href="/wiki/Kwik-E-Mart" title="Kwik-E-Mart">Kwik-E-Mart</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Convenience_store" title="Convenience store">convenience store</a> chain <a href="/wiki/7-Eleven" title="7-Eleven">7-Eleven</a> <a href="/wiki/Kwik-E-Mart#7-Eleven_promotion" title="Kwik-E-Mart">transformed 11 of its stores</a> in the U.S. and one in Canada into <a href="/wiki/Kwik-E-Mart" title="Kwik-E-Mart">Kwik-E-Marts</a>, at the cost of approximately <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">$</a>10 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-E.21_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-E.21-60">[60]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOX_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOX-61">[61]</a></sup> 7-Eleven also sold <i>Simpsons</i>-themed merchandise in many of its stores. This included "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_products_in_The_Simpsons#Squishee" title="List of products in The Simpsons">Squishees</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_products_in_The_Simpsons#Buzz_Cola" title="List of products in The Simpsons">Buzz Cola</a>", "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_products_in_The_Simpsons#Krusty-O.27s" title="List of products in The Simpsons">Krusty-O's</a>" Cereal, and "Pink Movie Donuts".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOX_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-FOX-61">[61]</a></sup> This promotion resulted in a 30% increase in profits for the altered 7-Eleven stores.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tieins_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-tieins-62">[62]</a></sup> Homer performed a special animated opening monologue for the July 24, 2007 edition of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_with_Jay_Leno" title="The Tonight Show with Jay Leno">The Tonight Show with Jay Leno</a></i>, as part of another promotion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>Promotions also occurred around the world. 20th Century Fox erected a "giant pink donut" in the town of <a href="/wiki/Springfield,_New_Zealand" title="Springfield, New Zealand">Springfield</a> in <a href="/wiki/Canterbury,_New_Zealand" title="Canterbury, New Zealand">Canterbury, New Zealand</a> to celebrate being named Springfield,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> while in London a double decker-sized floating inflatable Spider Pig was set up by the <a href="/wiki/Battersea_Power_Station" title="Battersea Power Station">Battersea Power Station</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Dorset" title="Dorset">Dorset</a>, England, an image of Homer was painted next to the <a href="/wiki/Hill_figure" title="Hill figure">hill figure</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cerne_Abbas_Giant" title="Cerne Abbas Giant">Cerne Abbas Giant</a>. This caused outrage amongst local <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Paganism_(contemporary)" title="Paganism (contemporary)">neopagans</a> who performed "rain magic" to try to get it washed away.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/McFarlane_Toys" title="McFarlane Toys">McFarlane Toys</a> released a line of action figures based on the film,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Electronic_Arts" title="Electronic Arts">EA Games</a> released <i><a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_Game" title="The Simpsons Game">The Simpsons Game</a></i>, to coincide with the film's DVD release, although the plot of the game was not based on the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Samsung" title="Samsung">Samsung</a> released <i>The Simpsons Movie</i> phone,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> produced a limited edition <i>The Simpsons Movie</i> <a href="/wiki/Xbox_360" title="Xbox 360">Xbox 360</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ben_%26_Jerry%27s" title="Ben &amp; Jerry's">Ben &amp; Jerry's</a> created a <i>Simpsons</i>-themed beer and donut-flavored ice cream, entitled "Duff &amp; D'oh! Nuts".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Windows_Live_Messenger" title="Windows Live Messenger">Windows Live Messenger</a> presented their users with the opportunity to download a free animated and static content for use within their conversations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Burger_King" title="Burger King">Burger King</a> produced a line of <i>Simpsons</i> toy figures that were given away with children's meals, and ran a series of <i>Simpsons</i>-themed television adverts to promote this.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tieins_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-tieins-62">[62]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JetBlue_Airways" title="JetBlue Airways">JetBlue Airways</a> held a series of online <a href="/wiki/Sweepstakes" title="Sweepstakes">sweepstakes</a> to win a trip to the film's <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a> premiere. They also included a channel dedicated to <i>The Simpsons</i> on their planes' <a href="/wiki/In-flight_entertainment" title="In-flight entertainment">in-flight entertainment</a> system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tieins_62-2"><a href="#cite_note-tieins-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_media">Home media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Simpsons_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Home media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Empire_State_Building_yellow.jpg"><img alt="Some buildings. The one at the back is yellow at the top." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="600" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Empire_State_Building_yellow.jpg/170px-Empire_State_Building_yellow.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Empire_State_Building_yellow.jpg/255px-Empire_State_Building_yellow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Empire_State_Building_yellow.jpg/340px-Empire_State_Building_yellow.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Empire_State_Building_yellow.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Empire_State_Building" title="Empire State Building">Empire State Building</a> was illuminated yellow to promote the film's home video release.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The film was released on <a href="/wiki/DVD" title="DVD">DVD</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray Disc</a> worldwide on December 3, 2007 and on December 18, 2007 in the U.S. It contains <a href="/wiki/Audio_commentary" title="Audio commentary">commentary</a> tracks from both the producers and animators, six short <a href="/wiki/Deleted_scene" title="Deleted scene">deleted scenes</a>, and a selection of material used to promote the film release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> An unfinished deleted scene of the townspeople singing the Springfield Anthem was also included on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_10)#DVD_release" title="The Simpsons (season 10)">The Simpsons The Complete Tenth Season</a></i> DVD boxset.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>Promotions for the DVD release occurred across the United States. The <a href="/wiki/Empire_State_Building" title="Empire State Building">Empire State Building</a> was illuminated yellow, the first time the building had ever been used as part of a film promotion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dvd_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-dvd-77">[77]</a></sup> In the United Kingdom, <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a> launched a £5 million advertising campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> They also signed a £1.6 million deal with the <a href="/wiki/Yogurt" title="Yogurt">yogurt</a> company <a href="/wiki/Yoplait" title="Yoplait">Yoplait</a>, to produce a <i>The Simpsons Movie</i> design for their brand <a href="/wiki/Go-Gurt" title="Go-Gurt">Frubes</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> In its first week it topped the U.S. DVD chart, and generated $11.8 million in rental revenue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dvd_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-dvd-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Simpsons_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Simpsons_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>The Simpsons Movie</i> received positive reviews. The film currently holds an 88% approval rating on <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a>, based on 220 reviews, with an average rating of 7.5/10. The site's critical consensus reads, "<i>The Simpsons Movie</i> contains the hearty laughs, biting satire, and honest portrayal of an American family that makes the show so popular. And it boasts slicker animation and polished writing that hearkens back to the show's glory days."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> On <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, it received a score of 80 out of 100, based on 36 critics, indicating "generally favorable reviews".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>British newspapers <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Times" title="The Times">The Times</a></i> both gave the film four out of five stars. <i>The Times</i>' James Bone said that it "boasts the same sly cultural references and flashes of brilliance that have earned the television series a following that ranges from tots to comparative literature PhDs".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> <i>The Guardian</i>'s Peter Bradshaw stated that it "gives you everything you could possibly want" and that he thought, "Eighty-five minutes [was] not long enough to do justice to 17 years of comedy genius".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> Ed Gonzalez praised the film for its political message, likening the <i>Itchy &amp; Scratchy</i> cartoon at the beginning to President Schwarzenegger's situation later on, as well as the film's visual gags.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gonzalez_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-gonzalez-41">[41]</a></sup> Randy Shulman praised the cast, and described them as having "elevated their vocal work to a craft that goes way beyond simple line readings", and particularly praised Kavner who he said "gave what must be the most heartfelt performance ever".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a> gave a positive review, but admitted he was "generally [not] a fan of movies spun off from TV animation". He called it "radical and simple at the same time, subversive and good-hearted, offensive without really meaning to be".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Richard_Corliss" title="Richard Corliss">Richard Corliss</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> said that the film "doesn't try to be ruder or kinkier, just bigger and better".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Julie_Kavner_1974.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="887" data-file-width="745" height="202" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Julie_Kavner_1974.JPG/170px-Julie_Kavner_1974.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Julie_Kavner_1974.JPG/255px-Julie_Kavner_1974.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Julie_Kavner_1974.JPG/340px-Julie_Kavner_1974.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Julie_Kavner_1974.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Julie_Kavner" title="Julie Kavner">Julie Kavner</a> was praised for her emotional performance as Marge and was nominated for an <a href="/wiki/Annie_Award" title="Annie Award">Annie Award</a> for voice acting.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i> film critic Claudia Puig said that the story did "warrant a full-length feature, thanks to a clever plot and non-stop irreverent humor".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Patrick Kolan believed that the film was "easily the best stuff to come [from the <i>Simpsons</i>] since <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_12)" title="The Simpsons (season 12)">season 12</a> or <a href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_(season_13)" title="The Simpsons (season 13)">13</a>" and praised the animation, but also said that the appearances of characters such as <a href="/wiki/Comic_Book_Guy" title="Comic Book Guy">Comic Book Guy</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Seymour_Skinner" title="Seymour Skinner">Seymour Skinner</a> were "small and unfunny".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> Kirk Honeycutt of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a></i> praised the film's good nature, stating that the laughs "come in all sizes", but also noted that, "little has been gained bringing the Simpsons to the screen."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup></p>
