<p><i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i>'s Brian Lowry called it "clever, irreverent, satirical and outfitted" but that it was "just barely" capable of sustaining a running time longer than a television episode.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Lisa Schwarzbaum praised the voice cast but stated that the "'action' sequences sometimes falter".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> When comparing the film to the early episodes of the show, Stephen Rowley concluded that the film "has more going for it than the show in its later years, but is still a long way short of what made it so invigorating".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Monthly" title="The Monthly">The Monthly</a></i> critic <a href="/wiki/Luke_Davies" title="Luke Davies">Luke Davies</a> echoed Lowry's concerns about the length: "everything moves with the whip-crack speed of a half-hour episode. And that's the paradox: it makes the film feel like three episodes strung together. We're in a cinema, and we expect something epic." He opined that "in the great arc that is the history of <i>The Simpsons</i>, this film will come to be seen as oddity rather than apotheosis."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>More negative reception came from the magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i>, where reviewer Ian Nathan compared the film to <a href="/wiki/New_Coke" title="New Coke">New Coke</a>, saying that "it utterly failed".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-empirereview_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-empirereview-42">[42]</a></sup> Phil Villarreal believed that there were "too few laugh-worthy moments" and that "instead of stretching to new frontiers, the film rests on the familiar".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> Sheila Johnston criticized the pacing of the film and its joke level saying that "the overall momentum flags at times" and that it was "a salvo of comic squibs, some very funny, others limp".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> David Edwards agreed with this, writing that although "there's a great half-hour show rattling around...the rest is padding at its very dullest", concluding that it "isn't a terrible film, just a terribly disappointing one."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cosmo_Landesman" title="Cosmo Landesman">Cosmo Landesman</a> believed, "the humour seem[ed] to have lost its satirical bite and wit" and that "much of the comedy is structured around the idiocy of Homer".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> This assessment was shared by Carina Chocano of the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i>, who felt that "once the movie wanders into its contemplation of mortality and meaning, the trenchancy kind of creaks and falls off." She negatively compared it to <i><a href="/wiki/South_Park:_Bigger,_Longer_%26_Uncut" title="South Park: Bigger, Longer &amp; Uncut">South Park: Bigger, Longer &amp; Uncut</a></i> (1999), a film similarly adapted from an animated television series, saying that, in terms of satire, it offers "nothing we don't hear every night on <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Daily_Show_with_Jon_Stewart" title="The Daily Show with Jon Stewart">The Daily Show with Jon Stewart</a></i>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> Bruce Newman criticized the fleeting appearances of many of the show's secondary characters, and found the film to be "a disappointment".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office">Box office</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Simpsons_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Box office">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The film earned $30,758,269 on its opening day in the U.S. making it the 25th-highest, and fifth-highest non-sequel opening day revenue of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> It grossed a combined total of $74,036,787 in its opening weekend on 5,500 screens at 3,922 theaters, reaching the top of the box office for that weekend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> This made it the tenth-highest revenue of all time, for an opening weekend in July, and highest among non-sequels, and the highest animated TV adaptation of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> This outperformed the expectations of $40 million that Fox had for the release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<p>It set several American box office records, including highest grossing opening weekend for a non-<a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">CG</a> animated film and for a film based on a television series, surpassing <i><a href="/wiki/Mission:_Impossible_II" title="Mission: Impossible II">Mission: Impossible II</a></i>. It was also the third-highest grossing opening weekend for an animated film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> It opened at the top of the international box office taking $96 million from 71 overseas territories, including $27.8 million in the United Kingdom, the second-highest UK opening ever for a <a href="/wiki/20th_Century_Fox" title="20th Century Fox">20th Century Fox</a> film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> It contributed to over half of the record 5.5 million people attending British cinemas that weekend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> In Australia, it grossed <a href="/wiki/Australian_dollar" title="Australian dollar">$</a>13.2 million, the third-highest opening weekend in the country, and the highest for an animated film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> The United Kingdom is the highest-grossing country for the film outside the US with a $78,426,654 gross overall, with Germany in second place with a $36,289,250 gross overall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup> The film closed on December 20, 2007 with a gross of $183,135,014 in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a> and a worldwide gross of $527,068,706. It was the eighth-highest-grossing film worldwide and the twelfth-highest grossing in the United States and Canada of 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-box_office_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-box_office-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Simpsons_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_The_Simpsons#Awards_for_The_Simpsons_Movie" title="List of awards and nominations received by The Simpsons">List of awards and nominations received by The Simpsons Movie</a></div>
<p><i>The Simpsons Movie</i> won the award for Best Comedy Film at the <a href="/wiki/British_Comedy_Awards" title="British Comedy Awards">British Comedy Awards</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> Best Animation at the inaugural <a href="/wiki/ITV_(TV_network)" title="ITV (TV network)">ITV</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Movie_Awards" title="National Movie Awards">National Movie Awards</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> and Best Movie at the UK <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nickelodeon_Kids_Choice_Awards" title="Nickelodeon Kids Choice Awards">Nickelodeon Kids Choice Awards</a>, beating <i><a href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Order_of_the_Phoenix_(film)" title="Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix (film)">Harry Potter and the Order of the Phoenix</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Pirates_of_the_Caribbean:_At_World%27s_End" title="Pirates of the Caribbean: At World's End">Pirates of the Caribbean: At World's End</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Shrek_the_Third" title="Shrek the Third">Shrek the Third</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> The film's trailer won a Golden Trailer Award in the category Best Animated/Family Film Trailer at the 8th Annual Golden Trailer Awards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> named the film the third best of the year, based on its box office takings and <i>Metacritic</i> critical response score.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> The film's website received a <a href="/wiki/Webby_Award" title="Webby Award">Webby Award</a> at the 12th Annual Webby Awards in the category "Best Movie and Film Website".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/35th_Annie_Awards" title="35th Annie Awards">35th Annie Awards</a> the film was nominated in four categories: <a href="/wiki/Annie_Award_for_Best_Animated_Feature" title="Annie Award for Best Animated Feature">Best Animated Feature</a>, Directing in an Animated Feature Production, Writing in an Animated Feature Production, and Voice Acting in an Animated Feature Production for <a href="/wiki/Julie_Kavner" title="Julie Kavner">Julie Kavner</a>. All four awards were won by <i><a href="/wiki/Ratatouille_(film)" title="Ratatouille (film)">Ratatouille</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> It was nominated for <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Animated_Feature_Film" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Animated Feature Film">Best Animated Feature Film</a> at the <a href="/wiki/65th_Golden_Globe_Awards" title="65th Golden Globe Awards">65th Golden Globe Awards</a>, the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Film_and_Television_Arts" title="British Academy of Film and Television Arts">BAFTA</a> for <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Animated_Film" title="BAFTA Award for Best Animated Film">Best Animated Film</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Producers_Guild_of_America_Awards_2007" title="Producers Guild of America Awards 2007">Producers Guild Award</a> for Animated Theatrical Motion Picture.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> It also received nominations for the <a href="/wiki/Satellite_Award_for_Best_Animated_or_Mixed_Media_Feature" title="Satellite Award for Best Animated or Mixed Media Feature">Satellite Award for Best Animated or Mixed Media Feature</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chicago_Film_Critics_Association_Award_for_Best_Animated_Feature" title="Chicago Film Critics Association Award for Best Animated Feature">Chicago Film Critics Association Award for Best Animated Feature</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_Film_Critics_Association" title="Broadcast Film Critics Association">Broadcast Film Critics Association</a> Award for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Broadcast_Film_Critics_Association_Award_for_Best_Animated_Feature" title="Broadcast Film Critics Association Award for Best Animated Feature">Best Animated Feature</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>Before its release, the film received a nomination at the <a href="/wiki/2007_MTV_Movie_Awards" title="2007 MTV Movie Awards">2007 MTV Movie Awards</a> for "Best Summer Movie You Haven't Seen Yet", with the award ultimately won by <i><a href="/wiki/Transformers_(film)" title="Transformers (film)">Transformers</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> and lost the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teen_Choice_Award" title="Teen Choice Award">Teen Choice Award</a> for "Choice Summer Movie – Comedy/Musical", which was won by <i><a href="/wiki/Hairspray_(2007_film)" title="Hairspray (2007 film)">Hairspray</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> It was also nominated for Favorite Movie Comedy at the <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Choice_Awards" title="People's Choice Awards">People's Choice Awards</a>, losing to <i><a href="/wiki/Knocked_Up" title="Knocked Up">Knocked Up</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Possible_sequel">Possible sequel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Simpsons_Movie&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Possible sequel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2014, James L. Brooks stated that he had been approached by Fox and that they had requested a second film. He added that there were no immediate plans, stating: "We've been asked to [develop it], but we haven't. We're doing a lot of other stuff."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2015, just prior to the broadcast of the episode "<a href="/wiki/The_Man_Who_Came_to_Be_Dinner" title="The Man Who Came to Be Dinner">The Man Who Came to Be Dinner</a>", Al Jean and David Mirkin took to Twitter to reveal that the episode (which had been produced in 2012 and was originally set to air on May 19, 2013<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup>) had been held back<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> because it was being "seriously considered" for adaptation into a sequel film<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> as the episode was "very cinematic"; they cited a similar sequence of events that occurred earlier in the show's run with the episode "<a href="/wiki/Kamp_Krusty" title="Kamp Krusty">Kamp Krusty</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Jean also stated that he was sure reasons the episode both could and would not work as a film would occur to those that viewed the episode<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> and later expanded that there was the fear of the potential film being considered "not canonical" with the TV series<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> and the potential backlash of overcoming it by using a "memory wipe".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
